  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fd0f43f0-b9bc-4d3b-bbbc-bb9cd775fc7c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

Caged behind an electrical fence, locked in a house in the middle of the snow, Senna is left to decode the clues to find out why she was taken. If she wants her freedom, she has to take a close look at her past. But, her past has a heartbeat... and her kidnapper is nowhere to be found. With her survival hanging by a thread, Senna soon realizes this is a game. A dangerous one. Only the truth can set her free.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_679068630" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679068630" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679068630?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679068630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13741975358467677617"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396798439i/9188216._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That’s what it’s like to be a prisoner of anything. You want your freedom until you get it, then you feel bare without your chains.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Woah.<br/><br/>That was pretty much my response after finishing this book. Just woah. I didn’t even know what to say about it. What could I say that would properly convey my feelings about this book? I felt like my review should just have been 3 words and 2 hashtags:<br/><br/><b>JUST READ IT. #BringTissues #ItsComplicated </b><br/><br/>There are very few authors in the world whose books I</span>
  <span id="freeText13741975358467677617" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396798439i/9188216._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That’s what it’s like to be a prisoner of anything. You want your freedom until you get it, then you feel bare without your chains.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Woah.<br><br>That was pretty much my response after finishing this book. Just woah. I didn’t even know what to say about it. What could I say that would properly convey my feelings about this book? I felt like my review should just have been 3 words and 2 hashtags:<br><br><b>JUST READ IT. #BringTissues #ItsComplicated </b><br><br>There are very few authors in the world whose books I will go into blind. Tarryn Fisher is one of them. She earned my trust with the Love Me With Lies series but in a different way than most authors. I basically just came to understand that the stories I’d get from her would be fantastically well-written and completely outside the box. I guess I felt a certain safety in that in a weird way — like, knowing it was outside the box allowed me the mental freedom to just let go of the things I usually hold onto and just experience the story for what it was. I will admit though that she told me to expect a "<i>non-traditional ending</i>" before I started and I think knowing that allowed me to just stop worrying, stop expecting something in particular from it and just read it for what it was. And as for what it was ….. well, it was one hell of an amazing story.<br><br><blockquote>When reclusive novelist Senna Richards wakes up on her thirty-third birthday, everything has changed. Caged behind an electrical fence, locked in a house in the middle of the snow, Senna is left to decode the clues to find out why she was taken. If she wants her freedom, she has to take a close look at her past. But, her past has a heartbeat…and her kidnapper is nowhere to be found. With her survival hanging by a thread, Senna soon realizes this is a game. A dangerous one. <i><b>Only the truth can set her free.</b></i>
</blockquote><br><br>Mud Vein is not a fairy tale and honestly, it’s not really a romance either (at least not in the traditional way) even though it has very strong elements of love woven throughout it. The story unfolds in layers upon layers going forward and backward in time. With each layer, you discover a little more about the characters and what had shaped their lives. Some layers answered questions, others brought up new ones and, throughout it all, I remained riveted to the story.<br><br>I’m not going to say anything about the plot here and my strong advice is not to look up any spoilers. If you decide to read it, just dive right in. I’m the kind of reader who loves knowing in advance but I just dove in and loved my reading experience. But I will say that when you read it, <i>pay attention to everything.</i><br><br>The story itself drew me in from the first page. By the end of the first chapter, my mind was spinning. By the end of the second one, I had full body shivers and was desperately trying to figure out what was happening. My mind was filled with questions and the more I discovered, the more questions I had.<br><br>I also just want to point out that despite the fact that there is a kidnapping, this is not a ‘disturbing’ story. It does have darker, very adult themes but more than anything, it’s a complex journey of self discovery.<br><br>The story built in a very quiet way — it subtly snuck up on me, and when a tiny piece of the puzzle came into the light, it was epic. It hit me so hard. We’re talking chills, tears, everything.<br><br>Tarryn Fisher has an incredible talent for creating deeply flawed and complex characters that work their way into your heart. Regardless of whether you identify with them, you feel for them. You become wrapped up in their journey and you just feel connected. This book is cleverly written and perfectly paced. The layers built and wove together to create an intricate tale about what happens when the human mind and heart is put to a survival test.<br><br>When I was finished I just sat there with a heavy heart thinking back over the story. It hurt. As Tarryn has said, it was a <i>non-traditional ending</i>. But at the same time, it felt fitting for story. I went back and forth between denial and acceptance. I think sometimes though it’s about the journey, not the ending.<br><br>I give <i>Mud Vein</i> 5 stars for being incredibly well written, for stepping outside the box, for making me think, for making me feel (even if at times, I didn’t want to feel what I was feeling), and last but not least, for reminding me to appreciate every single moment of life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“There is a string that connects us that is not visible to the eye. Maybe every person has more than one soul they are connected to, and all over the world there are those invisible strings… Maybe the chances that you’ll find each and every one of your soul mates is slim. But sometimes you’re lucky enough to stumble across one. And you feel a tug. And it’s not so much a choice to love them though their flaws and through your differences, but rather you love them without even trying. You love their flaws.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>PS — if you want a feeling for the story listen to <i>Landscape</i> and <i>Cosmic Love</i> by Florence + The Machine.<br><br>PPS -- Many of you know that I like a very specific kind of book (and mostly they're only romance). <b>
  <u>This is not a romance novel</u>
</b> and I did not rate it "as" a romance. Everything about my preferences was thrown out the window when I read this book. I just went into it ready to accept whatever it was about and I strongly urge you to do the same.<br><br>****************************<br><br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13741975358467677617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_722909003" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722909003" />
    <a title="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei"><img alt="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421992465p2/2551178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722909003?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" href="/user/show/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei">Lady Vigilante (Feifei)</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722909003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8032724799213513136"><b>2 STARS - biggest disappointment of the year</b> <br/><br/>Where do I even begin?<br/><br/>Well, since part of my excitement to read this book was seeing the “Mud Vein faces” plastered all over my Facebook feed, I suppose I could show you my Mud Vein Face (actually there are two). <br/><br/><u>Mud Vein Face #1:</u><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397068143i/9226115.jpg' width='250' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This face is appropriate for the first 60% of the book.<br/><br/><u>Mud Vein Face #2:</u><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397068143i/9226116.jpg' width='250' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This face is appropriate for the last 40% of the book.<br/><br/><u>Book rating breakdown:</u><br/><br/><b>Writing:</b> 3<br/><b>Story:</b> 1<br/><b>Emotion:</b> 3<br/><b>Concept:</b> 2<br/><b>Steam:</b> 0 <br/><b>Believability:</b> 0<br/><b>Senna:</b> 1<br/><b>Isaac:</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8032724799213513136" style="display:none"><b>2 STARS - biggest disappointment of the year</b> <br><br>Where do I even begin?<br><br>Well, since part of my excitement to read this book was seeing the “Mud Vein faces” plastered all over my Facebook feed, I suppose I could show you my Mud Vein Face (actually there are two). <br><br><u>Mud Vein Face #1:</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397068143i/9226115.jpg" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This face is appropriate for the first 60% of the book.<br><br><u>Mud Vein Face #2:</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397068143i/9226116.jpg" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This face is appropriate for the last 40% of the book.<br><br><u>Book rating breakdown:</u><br><br><b>Writing:</b> 3<br><b>Story:</b> 1<br><b>Emotion:</b> 3<br><b>Concept:</b> 2<br><b>Steam:</b> 0 <br><b>Believability:</b> 0<br><b>Senna:</b> 1<br><b>Isaac:</b> 3<br><b>Did I like this book:</b> No.<br><br>If you asked me what makes Tarryn Fisher stand out from the rest of the authors, I’d say her writing. Sadly, not even her writing was a plus in Mud Vein. I found it to be overdescriptive and really just suffocated on all the extra details that hid what could’ve been a unique and well-delivered plot. <br><br>I’m not completely immune; I did find some lines in the book to be immensely powerful and they even gave me goosebumps. But taking in the book as a whole and considering the delivery, the reasoning, the revelation, and the endgame, I pretty much felt fucked over. And let me tell you, it’s not a good feeling.<br><br><b>1. Delivery.</b> The way I see it, there are two sides. One, I’m a complete idiot who lacks a brain because the first 60% I just. Did. Not. Get. (Refer to my Mud Vein Face #1). OR, the writing was so incredibly complex and just not understandable to mere humans only the writing goddess herself and a select few can interpret the meaning. Hence I didn’t find the writing beautiful; I thought it exorbitant and excessive. <br><br><b>2. Reasoning.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393309243ra/8692447.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It turns out Senna’s therapist/shrink is the one to kidnap her and Isaac and throw them in the cabin. And for what? So Senna could realize that she <i>can</i> love someone? So the shrink lady can play around with people’s lives? Oh and when they get discovered, Ms. Shrink Lady kills herself. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397068143ra/9226117.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So what was the point?<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Nothing about the reasoning made sense. It was neither plausible nor believable.<br><br><b>3. Revelation.</b> I wasn’t mindfucked, shocked, aghast, overwhelmed or anything. All that went through my head was OK. <br><br><b>4. Endgame.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386771574ra/7439882.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just can’t.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don’t mind that Senna died. Sometimes I find non-HEA books to be more meaningful and that certainly was the case with Mud Vein. Like I said, I’m not completely immune to the book. But oh my god. My biggest question I want an answer to is this:<br><br>Why is it that Senna is so deserving of love she must be locked in with Issac? Why is Issac’s wife and child not worthy of that love? WHY THE FUCK screw over a perfectly great family just so selfish, cold-hearted, rude, abrasive, shrewish Senna could get it huh? And please don’t tell me the shrink lady was crazy or that Senna deserves love just once because she’s dying from cancer. Not even <i>cancer</i> gets a pass on this.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Before I started this book, I purposely avoided reading the reviews so I could go in with a fresh, clean slate. In hindsight, I wished I read them before and listened to what friends were saying because this book has marred the perfect track record Fisher had with me.<br><br>That.Is.All. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397068143ra/9226118.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8032724799213513136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/807366770" />
    <a title="Patrycja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja"><img alt="Patrycja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586460589p2/6852653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/807366770?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrycja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrycja" href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja">Patrycja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer807366770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4272955383312045547"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420433._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='40' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Title:</b> Mud Vein<br/><b>Series:</b> Standalone<br/><b>Author:</b> Tarryn Fisher<br/><b>Release Date: </b> 6th April, 2014<br/><b>Rating:</b> 1 stars<br/><b>Cliffhanger:</b>. No<br/><b> HEA: </b> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ No  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420434._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='40' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>I have no idea how to properly review this book without giving away huge spoilers; it’s almost impossible to do so. But as I want to explain step by step what made me hate Tarryn Fisher’s novel I will divide my review .First part of it will be short and to the point and you can read it without worrying about reading spoilers. Second one will</span>
  <span id="freeText4272955383312045547" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420433._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Title:</b> Mud Vein<br><b>Series:</b> Standalone<br><b>Author:</b> Tarryn Fisher<br><b>Release Date: </b> 6th April, 2014<br><b>Rating:</b> 1 stars<br><b>Cliffhanger:</b>. No<br><b> HEA: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ No  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420434._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>I have no idea how to properly review this book without giving away huge spoilers; it’s almost impossible to do so. But as I want to explain step by step what made me hate Tarryn Fisher’s novel I will divide my review .First part of it will be short and to the point and you can read it without worrying about reading spoilers. Second one will be complex explanation and will contain spoilers. So you can decide if you want to still read it and see what this mind fuck was all about. <br> <br><b>
  <blockquote>5 stages of BOOK DENIAL<br><br><br>FIRST PART OF REVIEW –</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Reading Mud Vein was a challenge. One, that did not end on a positive note for me– not only was I completely astounded by how incredibly idiotic the plot seemed, I hated the characters also. Everything was so unrealistic and naïve and unlikely to happen I WANTED TO DIE. But I will get there. <br><br>Anyway, I was very excited to finally dive into Fisher’s book. I haven’t read her other series, because I am not a fan of love triangles etc. but hearing many awesome things about her writing style I knew I had to read her other books. So being exceptionally giddy and full of hope I cracked this story open… and… and… I felt thoroughly fucked, but not in pleasant way. <br><br>I have never in my entire life read a book I haven’t understood. I’ve read many stupid, dumb books, I’ve read books I hated, books terribly written, but I have never ever did not get what it was about, and here I just didn’t get the message. If someone would ask me what was the point of writing Mud Vein or what kind of story it is, I wouldn’t be able to answer this questions. I honestly don’t know. I feel like the dumbest chick, but seriously if there is a person who could explain this book to me, I would love to hear it. <br><br>On the other hand, I have to underline that I found Tarryn Fisher's writing spellbinding. She's very talented author and some of the things she wrote gave me goosebumbs. I can understand her need to explore darker corners of minds. Big plus for that as I appriciate uniqueness and honesty. Sadly, it just didn't work for me. And I wish it did.<br><br>SECOND PART – SPOILERS!!!SERIOUS ONES!!! <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>Okay, let’s get this ball rolling.<br><br>Senna is a captive along with Isaac in a closed house, somewhere in the middle of nowhere. They can’t leave the building at all, but have everything what is need to stay alive (food, clothes, water, warmth etc.) They don’t know why and what’s the point of it. So they wait for their captor to make himself/herself known. It doesn’t happen. They are closed for weeks. <br><br>Why Mud Vein is a MIND FUCK?<br><br>-	Isaac has a wife and expects baby but still sleeps with Senna (I know, horrible, but nothing we haven’t seen before, right?)<br>-	Senna was raped few years before her kidnapping, and then she found out she had a breast cancer (almost the same day)<br>-	Senna went a little bit crazy<br>-	The captive thing was a psychological experiment her psychiatrist arranged, you know cause she’s a little sick too<br>-	Senna’s cancer spread while being captivated for months<br>-	Senna died (I came to this conclusion as the book ends with Goodbye letter)<br>-	Oh and yeah, Isaac declared his undying love<br><br>I have no more words. Seriously. NEEEEXT<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>TAADAAAM!<br><br>Yes, this is Mud Vein in nutshell. Shocked? Yeah me too. Dumbfounded? High five me. Don’t know what this book is about? Welcome in the freakin’ club. <br><br>I can understand if other people will call Mud Vein exceptional mind game that throws the reader of the loop and gave this book five stars. I won't agree with it, but I can see the appeal. <br><br>I won't say don't go for it, don't read it, because well that could really be bad if you passed it and enjoy dark and gritty and mysterious. I wasn't smart enough to get the message of Mud Vein, but you definitely CAN! <br><br><br><b>FOLLOW SMOKIN HOT BOOK BLOG ON: <b><br><br><a href="https://twitter.com/BlogSmokin/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="Twitter" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391768351i/8452934.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="http://facebook.com/smokinhotbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="Facebook" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391768485i/8452963.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://plus.google.com/113975606544004548659" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="Google Plus" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391768485i/8452964.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="http://smokinhotbookblog.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="Smokin Hot Book Blog" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391769122i/8453144.png" width="32" height="32" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="mailto:rock17@onet.eu" <div id="review_1703571849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703571849" />
    <a title="Bibi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi"><img alt="Bibi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602128191p2/33411728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703571849?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781310791079" href="/book/show/21890756-mud-vein">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33411728-bibi?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33411728-bibi?shelf=sinister-suspense">sinister-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703571849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11618247568344154336">*Major Spoilers*<br/><br/><blockquote><b>Look, I live in a 3rd world country and even as I write this review there's no power</b> and my Iphone's hotspot is the only reason I have internet connectivity. It's 4 in the morning and I've spent the last 6 hrs reading MV.<br/><br/><i>Why should you care about my 3rd world problems you ask? So you understand the lack of electricity did not deter me from reading this book until I had read the very last word</i>. Yup, the writing was superb. <br/><br/><b>Yet, I hated it</b>.<br/><br/>It was one big pity fest; both Isacc and S</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11618247568344154336" style="display:none">*Major Spoilers*<br /><br /><blockquote><b>Look, I live in a 3rd world country and even as I write this review there's no power</b> and my Iphone's hotspot is the only reason I have internet connectivity. It's 4 in the morning and I've spent the last 6 hrs reading MV.<br /><br /><i>Why should you care about my 3rd world problems you ask? So you understand the lack of electricity did not deter me from reading this book until I had read the very last word</i>. Yup, the writing was superb. <br /><br /><b>Yet, I hated it</b>.<br /><br />It was one big pity fest; both Isacc and Senna were caricatures, infused with too much *fall-on- a-sword* self-obsessive, narcissistic traits.<br /><br /><b>Let's start with Senna</b>. Her mother walked away when she was 9 and boyfriend left when she was 20 and although these 2 incidents are heartbreaking, I don't believe they are tragic. Yet, she CHOSE to objectify herself as a victim by living a colorless whitewashed life for close to 13 years.<br /><br /><b>Then comes Isaac</b> (nice name BTW); who CHOSE to martyr himself on the "altar of love" while knowing his love might remain unrequited. Well, of course, the bit@&amp; psycho *cough*, Senna, can not and will not love him rather she slaps his arse with a restraining order, on the very day he told her he loved her. He, of course, does what every smart man ought to do; moves on to marry a different woman.<br /><br />Fast forward a couple of years and the protagonists find themselves in a situation that may very well lead to their demise. In this, they need to figure out how to survive, trust and depend on each other. Maybe even disclose their feelings, if any. <b>But really, both protagonists were mirror images of each other, Senna the *woe is me* and Isaac the *save you I must*. Very Titanic-ish; maybe even Romeo and Juliet-ish, and we all know how those worked out</b>.<br /><br />They survive but the price was paid a little too late.<br /><br />While the aforementioned issues are irritating, it was the actual lack of dialogue that killed this book and I know there are cybertheorists postulating Isaac might have been an illusion from Senna's psychotic break. With all due respect, the very lack of dialogue invalidates that theory; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25379213.Marrow" title="Marrow by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Marrow</a>, by the same author, is a brilliant accounting of psychosis. <br /><br />A lot more occurred in this book and I implore others to read it; however, I found it excruciatingly boring.<br /><br />That being said, I've read other books (Fuck Love, The Opportunists) by Fisher which I loved to bits, and will continue to one-click her.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11618247568344154336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1176892808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1176892808" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1176892808?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=read-it-and-weep">read-it-and-weep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1176892808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16334147462244168807"><i>
  <b>“You'll feel me in the fall backwards."</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>Mud Vein</i> is one of those books that when you're done and you put it down the first thing that you think is "what the hell did I just read?", and that's a good thing. I'm going to rate this book, but I have no idea at the same time if the rating will be fitting... I just don't know. I can see why someone would rate this a one and why someone would rate this a ten.<br/><br/><i>Mud Vein</i> follows Senna, a recluse writer and Isaac, her ex. The two wake up locked away in a</span>
  <span id="freeText16334147462244168807" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“You'll feel me in the fall backwards."</b>
</i><br><br><i>Mud Vein</i> is one of those books that when you're done and you put it down the first thing that you think is "what the hell did I just read?", and that's a good thing. I'm going to rate this book, but I have no idea at the same time if the rating will be fitting... I just don't know. I can see why someone would rate this a one and why someone would rate this a ten.<br><br><i>Mud Vein</i> follows Senna, a recluse writer and Isaac, her ex. The two wake up locked away in a cabin in the woods. Neither of them remember how they got there, where they are, or why they are there. Despite their best efforts the two can't seem to escape. Senna is one of the most complex female protagonist I've ever read. She is a broken women. A sad women. Seeing everything as grey and empty. Senna is a female I think so many women can relate to, but again you might not be able to explain why. I personally felt this magnetic pull towards her. I constantly found myself wanting to know more about her. Senna's character was one of such little words, yet one that didn't need to speak all the time. It had me floored. Isaac, wow, he was a perfect male lead. I loved everything about him. I liked his light, his attitude, the way he was a nurturer, and how he was completely Senna's opposite. He is a leading male that I could spend so much time on gushing about. He is funny, sexy, charming, but someone that I feel (sadly) I can't go too in depth with. These two were day and night and their romance is gripping.<br><br><b>
  <i>“You’ve been silent your whole life. You were silent when we met, silent when you suffered. Silent when life kept hitting you. I was like that too, a little. But not like you. You are a stillness. And I tried to move you. It didn’t work. But that doesn’t mean you didn’t move me. I heard everything you didn’t say. I heard it so loudly that I couldn’t shut it off. Your silence, Senna, I hear it so loudly.”</i>
</b><br><br>The two of them will also drive you mad! Tarryn has it so that she reveals their traits in such a peppered way that you'll be thirsty to know more. I was so frustrated by them that at around the 20% mark of this book I almost threw in the towel and DNF'd it. However, my goodreads friends told me to push through and just make it to the end. The uphill battle was worth it. I don't know how you're able to full understand a character, but feel at the same time you don't know them at all. That's how Tarryn makes you feel the whole time. Any flaws in the plot is repaired by these two characters. That and the romance. The romance in this book was so bizarre and amazing. <br><br>The plot of <i>Mud Vein</i> is all over the place. It's a romantic thriller and reads to a T like one. There is always something happening even in its more "calm" moments. The whole book is bang after bang, twist after twist. It's timeline bounces around often, and at first this made reading a bit confusing. That might have been what was so off putting at first. The fact that things took a while to click just made pulling through this book a little rocky... Then again I also won't say that things ever full click. It's in present time, past tense, and even at one point in time is from some else's point of view. Those chapters, the Nick ones, were my favorite. They are flawless!!! I could read an entire book from his POV. The plot, though "messy", still manages to somehow be put together and it's twist is a complete blindside. I did not in any way, shape, or form see it coming... Don't get me wrong, you know it's coming, and you've been waiting 200 pages for it but good God... My brain short circuited for a minute and I forgot how to breathe.<br><br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-mPCyTzEDWT8/VyUVxNVjGEI/AAAAAAAADeo/yfobeGjctbsyShufqn7UGftS3UTcQeXrgCLcB/s1600/back%2Bit%2Bup.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="135" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462051400ra/18948679.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It's really genius... With that being said, there is also something missing about the ending. At first thought I didn't like it, but now having time to think about it I actually like how things are left off. <br><br><i>Mud Vein</i> will pull you in, tear you apart, make you miss something you didn't know existed, and then... leave you wanting more. <i>Mud Vein</i> is a flawed book, and that is exactly what makes it so wonderful. It's scattered, muddy, and oh so dark. The best part of this book is that it is so, SO quotable. So many lines from this story had me in tears and those powerful beautiful lines are what gives this book an extra kick.<br><br><b><i>“He kissed me with color, with drumbeat, and a surgeon’s precision. He kissed me with who he was, the sum of his life—and it was all encompassing. I wondered what I kissed him with since I was only broken parts.”</i><br><br>Tarryn Fisher will make you realize that you don't have to be the sun, that you can be the rain... and that's okay. <br><br><b> Read this review and others over on my blog<br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> </b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16334147462244168807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1664413217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664413217" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664413217?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=cute-book-couple">cute-book-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=fangirling">fangirling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=highly-recommended-na">highly-recommended-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=angst-overload">angst-overload</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=sobfest">sobfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=damn-this-guy-is-perfect">damn-this-guy-is-perfect</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=hot-male-characters">hot-male-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664413217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5313019468621813992"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"It's the darkness that pulls me in. Your mud vein."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>5 Stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher' title='Tarryn Fisher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tarryn Fisher</a>, you just left me speechless there!<br/><br/>This may be one of the best unsettling books I've read in my entire life. It's <b>dark and twisted</b>, chilling and psychotic, and totally riveting. Mind-blown!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450904166ra/17482914.gif' width='370' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Someone could take your body, use it, beat it, treat it like it's a piece of trash, but what hurts far worse than the actual physical attack is the darkness it injects in you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18246727.Mud_Vein' title='Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mud Vein</a> begins when <b>Senna Richards</b> </span>
  <span id="freeText5313019468621813992" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"It's the darkness that pulls me in. Your mud vein."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>5 Stars!</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher" title="Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Tarryn Fisher</a>, you just left me speechless there!<br><br>This may be one of the best unsettling books I've read in my entire life. It's <b>dark and twisted</b>, chilling and psychotic, and totally riveting. Mind-blown!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450904166ra/17482914.gif" width="370" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Someone could take your body, use it, beat it, treat it like it's a piece of trash, but what hurts far worse than the actual physical attack is the darkness it injects in you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18246727.Mud_Vein" title="Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Mud Vein</a> begins when <b>Senna Richards</b> woke up one day in a strange home. She didn't exactly remember what or who brought her there. She later on found out that she's not the only one who was abducted but also <b>Isaac Asterholder</b>, the surgeon who saved her from a traumatic incident months ago and the one who operated her breast cancer away. Together they did everything to survive in that inescapable place and tried to bring themselves out. But when days and weeks passed without getting any clue, their intricately deep and dark feelings were slowly unraveled which made their situation a lot more twisted.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I am an animal, bent on surviving. I let nothing in. I let nothing out."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>It's my second time to read a novel by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher" title="Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Tarryn Fisher</a>. The first one was her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25828204.F_ck_Love" title="F*ck Love by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">F*ck Love</a> which unfortunately didn't amaze me. I vowed to give her another chance after that and now I don't regret it. This one is going straight to my favorites!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I am a self-fulfilling prophecy; destroying before I could be destroyed."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>There were so many things that I loved about this book. First was of course, the <b>impeccable writing</b> of Tarryn that is all her own. I found myself so engaged because of the gripping quality of her writing. Secondly, the gasp-inducing thrilling scenes that the book brought. Also, the book had that certain effect, one that invited me to dig more and more to discover the mystery behind. It basically left my mind reeling in ten different directions all at once. Hands-down! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"That's what it's like to be a prisoner of anything. You want your freedom until you get it, then you feel bare without your chains."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>One of the things that also surprised me was the <b>romance</b>. I didn't thought the romantic aspect here had a bigger role in the entire story. Which was good, in my opinion because in the end, everything just made a perfect sense.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Being stuck on love was a real bitch to cure. Like cancer, I think. Just when you think you're over it, it comes back."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The <b>plot</b> also impressed me. I loved when the book took me from present to past and back to the present. It just made the mystery more and more interesting.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I never thought of love as a choice. Rather, it seemed like the un-choice. But if you stayed with someone who was self-destructing and chose to keep loving, I suppose it could be a choice."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>My favorite parts of course, were those scenes when Senna and Isaac interacted before they were kidnapped. Isaac was such a perfect hero. Just one of a kind. The gentleness he exuded and the way he did everything to stay by Senna's side after what happened to her was so admirable. I mean, damn, I can't help but fall for this man.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"If someone was going to be digging around in my chest with a scalpel, I wanted it to be the guy who showed up and fixed things."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>And then when this conversation happened...<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Why are you here?" <br>He hesitated briefly then said, "Because you are."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466249332i/19457610.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Senna, I admit, was difficult to understand. Her dark thoughts and her self-destructing personality made me cringe every time. But she was uniquely portrayed in this book and scrutinizing her way of thinking was the best thing of all.<br><br>There were lots of cry-worthy moments here. I felt so connected to the characters and their emotions and everything they went through together. There was just something about their insane experience that made me feel so emotional.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You are a stillness. And I tried to move you. It didn't work. But that doesn't mean you didn't move me. I heard everything you didn't say. I heard it so loudly that I couldn't shut it off. Your silence, Senna. I hear it so loudly."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Another scene that broke my heart into pieces...<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Tell me a lie, Isaac." His fingertips trace a curlicue on my shoulder.<br>"I don't love you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>This book was also <b>unpredictable</b>. I developed a lot of conspiracy theories but none of them was correct. Lol. I guess I'm just not a good detective.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You loved me so much that I started to love myself."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Overall, this <b>book was a real surprise</b>. It's a great psychological, romantic thriller. The ending of course, made me cry. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I admit I kind of hoped that there would be a happily ever after but anyway, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I think that conclusion was just the right way to end it. It was strongly delivered and it sure gave me goosebumps. I would highly recommend this amazing book for fans of dark and mystery/psychological suspense and thriller books.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You can't fix me," I said, looking at his knees. <br>"I don't want to."<br>"I'm mangled," I said. "On the inside and the outside."<br>"And yet I love you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><p>
  <a href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446199662i/16763926._SX540_.jpg" alt="Pearl's Book Journey (1)" width="380" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464648592i/19260109.png" width="250" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5313019468621813992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_745231457" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/745231457" />
    <a title="~ Becs ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2626261-becs"><img alt="~ Becs ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388693144p2/2626261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/745231457?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~ Becs ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~ Becs ~" href="/user/show/2626261-becs">~ Becs ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=dark-angsty">dark-angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745231457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5404120789350627888"><blockquote>Whether I shall turn out to be the hero of my own life, or whether that station will be held by anybody else, these pages must show.<br/><br/>~ Charles Dickens</blockquote><br/><br/>Well, it’s safe to say this book really did a number on me. I can sum up my experience in a few choice adjectives – shock, bewilderment, obsession, denial and sadness. It’s a painful read – one that will stay with you long after you close the last chapter. This book is so consuming that it seeped into my subconscious and lingered and festered there </span>
  <span id="freeText5404120789350627888" style="display:none"><blockquote>Whether I shall turn out to be the hero of my own life, or whether that station will be held by anybody else, these pages must show.<br><br>~ Charles Dickens</blockquote><br><br>Well, it’s safe to say this book really did a number on me. I can sum up my experience in a few choice adjectives – shock, bewilderment, obsession, denial and sadness. It’s a painful read – one that will stay with you long after you close the last chapter. This book is so consuming that it seeped into my subconscious and lingered and festered there corrupting my every thought and insidiously invading my dreams. This book will hurt you – Tarryn Fisher wields words like weapons and be prepared to lie wounded at her feet!<br><br>I was lucky enough to receive one of the earliest copies of Mud Vein for review and that blurb really isn’t giving much away. I didn’t know what to expect and I certainly didn’t get the book I anticipated. I think I thought I was heading down a dark erotic path but it’s really much more of a psychological thriller than anything else. In fact, at the beginning, it feels almost like a Saw movie with a bit of Stephen King’s Misery added into the mix but it very much comes into it’s own and it’s unlike anything I’ve ever read before.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396784138i/9186692._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo mudveinquotey_zps3aa63d4f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So take a wander into the unexpected, avoid all spoilers (you won’t find any here) and just experience this white knuckle ride the way the author intends.<br><br>As the blurb says, Senna awakens from a drug-induced slumber to find herself a prisoner in a house in the middle of a white wilderness of a snowy landscape with someone significant from her past. She has absolutely no clue why she is there and who is responsible for getting her there and she’s in profound shock, clutching knives as she sleeps, never knowing what may be coming next. The silence of that barren white wilderness outside is deafening as it feels as though she and her companion are the only two people left in the world – a bit like Adam and Even in the Garden of Eden although this is about as far from paradise as it is possible to be.<br><br>The desperation and bleakness of their situation is so beautifully handled as you go through the phases of shock and denial with them – I honestly read most of this book with a sense of bewilderment wanting to know who or why but I had no clue. I guessed several times and I never once guessed right who is responsible for all of this. I stumbled through this novel, never knowing what Tarryn Fisher might throw at you next as Senna’s tale both present and past is retold in harrowing detail.<br><br>Senna is such a spiky, anti-social individual. She’s really struggled to fit the social norms throughout her life and is now a reclusive novelist and pretty damaged individual. To say the girl gets no luck is a big understatement – Senna is delivered blow after blow and my heart went out to her, wishing she would accept comfort where it is offered and knowing she won’t. There’s a beautiful love out there for her but she’s too absorbed in her own pain, far too anti-social to ever reach out and take what is offered and only this evil incarceration will finally knock the scales from her eyes and allow her to truly ‘see’.<br><br>And this is where we get back to that sadness part – there is a whole load of missed opportunities in her life. Senna has had chances of happiness but never takes them – she made my heart hurt so badly. She’s such a lonely soul dwelling only in the darkness of her mind, never allowing anyone to get close, never accepting any comfort offered – she’s Difficult with a big old capital D and she broke my heart. <br><br>The author does a fantastic job of grabbing your attention right from page one and dragging you kicking and screaming through the story and then dropping you from a great height right at the end, leaving you in a bedraggled heap and nursing your wounds. This is going to hurt and leave you with a big book hangover. It’s dark and twisted and ultimately very sad and it’s an utterly compelling and completely captivating read. I was totally obsessed with this book during the days that I read it and it really did invade my dreams – I carried the dark, oppressive atmosphere of the it with me everywhere, even in my sleep.<br><br><br>I’ve read and enjoyed Tarryn Fisher before and, while this is a very different story from her Love Me With Lies trilogy, it is still delivered with her wholly addictive, dry, edgy style that I became so hooked on in the past. It’s definitely not the book I expected, it’s not a romance at all so be prepared for something different, go in blind and expect the unexpected and, most of all, be prepared for a painful ride.<br><br><b>5 dark and edgy stars</b><br><br><p><a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/2014/04/mud-vein-by-tarryn-fisher-release-day.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read this review at Sinfully Sexy</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sinfullysexybookreviews" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow us on Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/SinfullySexyB" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow us on Twitter</a></p><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5404120789350627888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText663126772154715065" style="display:none"><b>$.99 deal <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1szjRDq">http://amzn.to/1szjRDq</a></b><br>5/10/2014<br><br>Curious to find out why some friends DNF-ed this book while others LOVED it. <br><br>Let the mind games begin.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397839701i/9335304.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦✦<br>I've finished and I'm on the side that loved the story. <b>MUD VEIN</b> was more of a <b>psychological thriller</b> than a true romance. The plot is filled with twist and turns that will leave you piecing stuff together. One final piece of advice given by Dr. Elgin to everyone-<b> "Read the book."</b> If you like non-traditional books than you may like this one.<br><br><b>Standalone</b><br><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_challenges/1196247" rel="nofollow noopener">60th book for 2014</a></span>

<div id="review_904424952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904424952" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/904424952?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904424952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17801172083089165309">I have no words that will do any review of this story justice. This book made me feel things that no other book has ever came close to making me feel. All I really know is that this novel makes me feel guilty for giving any other novel a five star rating. <br/><br/>I can say that Tarryn Fisher has the most beautiful writing I've ever read. In my whole twenty-six years of existence, I have never read anything as beautiful. The last sentence on this book will probably haunt me for some time, and I look forw</span>
  <span id="freeText17801172083089165309" style="display:none">I have no words that will do any review of this story justice. This book made me feel things that no other book has ever came close to making me feel. All I really know is that this novel makes me feel guilty for giving any other novel a five star rating. <br><br>I can say that Tarryn Fisher has the most beautiful writing I've ever read. In my whole twenty-six years of existence, I have never read anything as beautiful. The last sentence on this book will probably haunt me for some time, and I look forward to it.<br><br>When I was describing this book and my feelings to my best friend, he made me realize I was experiencing a catharsis. It literally purged things out of me I didn't even know I had in me. It soothed me and put my mind at ease to darkness I knew I held inside. <br><br>I cried through most of this book, and the tears continued for about an hour afterwards. Not because it was sad, even though it was, but because of how real this book is. I just laid in bed and thought about how much this book took out of me, but how much more full it made me feel. <br><br>The closest book I can compare this to is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10956.The_Virgin_Suicides?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Virgin Suicides</a>, which I was obsessed with in high school even though I didn't get the real meaning until much later in life. Yet, even it does not hold a candle to this book. This book is unlike anything I've ever read. It's not a love story, PNR, great sex erotica, historical romance, it's not even the mystery novel the excerpt has you believe it is. This book is balancing your darkness but still letting your light in, even if you need someone to help you let it in. <br><br>Like I said, I really have no words for this. I can never thank <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7345713" rel="nofollow noopener">Paloma</a> enough for getting me to read this, despite the horrible reviews I kept seeing. If you want to <i>feel</i> something, I recommend this book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427704587i/14309333._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>^I was so in love, I had to get it signed ❤️.<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17801172083089165309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_681018612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681018612" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681018612?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681018612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11464412117449181503"><b>Initial Thoughts after reading: </b><br/><br/>Well that left me an utter mess. Not sure how to rate this yet. I'm still in the middle of piecing my heart back together. Review to come.<br/><br/><b>Final review:</b><br/>It pains me to write this review, because I LOVED Tarryn’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/85015-love-me-with-lies' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love Me With Lies series</a>. It’s one of my all time favorite series, one of the most memorable for me. While I can’t say <b>Mud Vein </b>was unmemorable, quite the opposite, I can’t stop thinking about it. The difference is, I wish I could. <br/><br/>My main reason for the low</span>
  <span id="freeText11464412117449181503" style="display:none"><b>Initial Thoughts after reading: </b><br /><br />Well that left me an utter mess. Not sure how to rate this yet. I'm still in the middle of piecing my heart back together. Review to come.<br /><br /><b>Final review:</b><br />It pains me to write this review, because I LOVED Tarryn’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/85015-love-me-with-lies" rel="nofollow noopener">Love Me With Lies series</a>. It’s one of my all time favorite series, one of the most memorable for me. While I can’t say <b>Mud Vein </b>was unmemorable, quite the opposite, I can’t stop thinking about it. The difference is, I wish I could. <br /><br />My main reason for the low rating is my feelings throughout the story. Mud Vein was not an enjoyable reading experience for me. I did not like Senna for the majority of the story, in fact I wanted to SHAKE her more than a few times! Yes, she had horrible things happen to her, I get that, I think she should have a pass on some of her behavior, but for the most part she was completely selfish. Senna was extended kindness over and over from Isaac and she threw it back on him over and over. Being so self-absorbed she ignored his sufferings and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[never showed she cared to know anything about him. By the time she recognizes this and finally admits she loves Isaac, it’s too little, WAY too late.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Love gone wrong, and missed opportunity in a spectacular fashion. By the time I got to the end, I ugly cried. Big time. But it was ugly crying from hurt and FRUSTRATION.<br /><br />Senna had lots of similarities to Olivia from <b>The Opportunist</b> that I felt she was just another version of her, minus the likable parts. <br /><br />I felt the need to read quickly to get the story over with, and I just can’t rate a book highly when I feel that way.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11464412117449181503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1526503358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1526503358" />
    <a title="Beth Hudspeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18107143-beth-hudspeth"><img alt="Beth Hudspeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495723320p2/18107143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1526503358?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Hudspeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Hudspeth" href="/user/show/18107143-beth-hudspeth">Beth Hudspeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=mind-fucks">mind-fucks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=grab-a-tissue">grab-a-tissue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=judging-by-the-cover">judging-by-the-cover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526503358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15883632530702519344"><blockquote>
  <blockquote>Review posted at: <a href='https://hellobeautifulbookblog.wordpress.com/2016/02/05/book-review-mud-vein-by-tarryn-fisher/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a></blockquote>
</blockquote><br/>A mud vein is the dark strip down the back of a shrimp. You have to take it out for it to be clean. The mud vein is the darkness. I think we all have a small one in us, some are more easily seen. Some wear their mud vein on their face, others try to cover it up with everything they can. <br/><br/>The landscape described in Mud Vein closely mirrors Senna. It is barren, it is solitude and silence, she is trapped in the landscape, but the landscape is her. There</span>
  <span id="freeText15883632530702519344" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <blockquote>Review posted at: <a href="https://hellobeautifulbookblog.wordpress.com/2016/02/05/book-review-mud-vein-by-tarryn-fisher/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a></blockquote>
</blockquote><br />A mud vein is the dark strip down the back of a shrimp. You have to take it out for it to be clean. The mud vein is the darkness. I think we all have a small one in us, some are more easily seen. Some wear their mud vein on their face, others try to cover it up with everything they can. <br /><br />The landscape described in Mud Vein closely mirrors Senna. It is barren, it is solitude and silence, she is trapped in the landscape, but the landscape is her. There is someone trapped there with her. Her savior, Isaac. He is essentially trapped within her and the landscape. She is holding him there and the landscape is holding him there. They have a tie that binds them together. If you are lucky enough to find this person in your life, never let them go, never take them for granted. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“What’s the difference?” I asked him. “Between the love of your life, and your soulmate?”<br />“One is a choice, and one is not.” </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I am going to put a disclaimer on this one. If you are going into this wanting a romance, you will not be happy. This book is hard to categorize. I also want to include the letter Tarryn wrote to readers of Mud Vein.<br /><br />Letter to the Readers about Mud Vein:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Dear Reader,<br />I am a writer and words are my weapon. I want to hurt you. I want my words to be salt, and I want to pour them into your open wound. I want my words to be jagged pieces of mirror that you can see yourself reflected in. I am a sadist otherwise known as an artist. My books are a call to women who have been doubled over by heartache, bound by boredom, captives of a past that will not let them go, victors of a past that tried to kill them. I have a disease you see, it’s called human nature, and I am fascinated by it. So, if you choose to read Mud Vein remember that about me. I’m not writing to entertain you, or to make money, or to have my book propped neatly on a shelf in Target. I write to explore the dark corners of myself, and I want you to come with me. I’m a little bit like you. I think you’ll see yourself in the pages of Mud Vein. I haven’t told you very much about it on purpose. I want you to go in blind. I want you to stumble across a thought, a sound, a hurt-which you had thought special to you. And realize I have felt them too, someone you have never met. If you choose to read Mud Vein, please don’t ask yourself what it says, ask yourself what it means. And once you read my black words, on a white page, e-mail me and tell me your interpretation. I can’t wait for your thoughts.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>“I am a writer and words are my weapon” – Tarryn Fisher</b><br />Truer words have never been spoken. Fisher wrecked my heart with this one. She opened my eyes. I love a book that you can’t get out of your head. It wasn’t the story-line, but the characters I can’t shake. The twist really didn’t surprise me, I pretty much had it figured out but it didn’t matter. I don’t care. It was the experience. It was being in Senna’s head and seeing a part of yourself there. It’s just a piece, but you know it’s there. It’s dark and twisted and mangled. Senna bore that on her body and in her mind. She never let anyone in and she never let anyone out. She is the electrical fence, she is the cabin, the fire, the carousel room, the attic, the snow. She is your depression and anger; she is the crazy you wish you could be when things go wrong. But in all that, she is BRAVE.<br /><br />Interesting it took this very dark book to break me out of my slump. This is my first 5 star review of this year and I’m about 16 books in. It evoked emotion in me. Emotions that are hard to describe. I felt raw reading this, I felt my face contort reading this, I felt my heart break reading this. Sometimes it's the pain that wakes us up, sometimes it's the pain that makes us feel anything and in turn, let's the happiness in. <br /><br />I think there is a small mud vein in us all.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"Cause she's just like the weather, can't hold her together<br />Born from dark water, daughter of the rain and snow"<br />--Florence and the Machine</b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15883632530702519344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
