<span id="freeTextContainer9228253554666355816"><a href='https://ibb.co/9ZMS1ZM' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595589791ra/29858022.gif' alt='ezgif-com-video-to-gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Wow, this book... fucking WOW!!!!!!! 💥💣💥💣<br/><br/>It's different, but ingenious...<br/>It's hard, but really fascinating...<br/>It's heart clenching, but wonderful...<br/>It is not standard but excellently written...<br/>It doesn't make much sense, but so special...<br/>It's unlike anything I've read before - and managed to completely undermine me!!! 😭😭😭<br/><br/>📚 "𝐖𝐡𝐚𝐭'𝐬 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐝𝐢𝐟𝐟𝐞𝐫𝐞𝐧𝐜𝐞?" 𝐈 𝐚𝐬𝐤𝐞𝐝 𝐡𝐢𝐦. "𝐁𝐞𝐭𝐰𝐞𝐞𝐧 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐥𝐨𝐯𝐞 𝐨𝐟 𝐲𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐥𝐢𝐟𝐞, 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐲𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐬𝐨𝐮𝐥𝐦𝐚𝐭𝐞?"<br/>"𝐎𝐧𝐞 𝐢𝐬 𝐚 𝐜𝐡𝐨𝐢𝐜𝐞, 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐨𝐧𝐞 𝐢𝐬 𝐧𝐨𝐭." 📚<br/><br/>I won't write anything about the plot, because </span>
  <span id="freeText9228253554666355816" style="display:none"><a href="https://ibb.co/9ZMS1ZM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595589791ra/29858022.gif" alt="ezgif-com-video-to-gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wow, this book... fucking WOW!!!!!!! 💥💣💥💣<br><br>It's different, but ingenious...<br>It's hard, but really fascinating...<br>It's heart clenching, but wonderful...<br>It is not standard but excellently written...<br>It doesn't make much sense, but so special...<br>It's unlike anything I've read before - and managed to completely undermine me!!! 😭😭😭<br><br>📚 "𝐖𝐡𝐚𝐭'𝐬 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐝𝐢𝐟𝐟𝐞𝐫𝐞𝐧𝐜𝐞?" 𝐈 𝐚𝐬𝐤𝐞𝐝 𝐡𝐢𝐦. "𝐁𝐞𝐭𝐰𝐞𝐞𝐧 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐥𝐨𝐯𝐞 𝐨𝐟 𝐲𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐥𝐢𝐟𝐞, 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐲𝐨𝐮𝐫 𝐬𝐨𝐮𝐥𝐦𝐚𝐭𝐞?"<br>"𝐎𝐧𝐞 𝐢𝐬 𝐚 𝐜𝐡𝐨𝐢𝐜𝐞, 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐨𝐧𝐞 𝐢𝐬 𝐧𝐨𝐭." 📚<br><br>I won't write anything about the plot, because it's one of those books that should be experienced on blind - but I'll just say that it's not for everyone - it's tragic and a bit depressing, but if you like psychological romance that will make you THINK and FEEL - this is a must-read book for you! 🎠<br><br>The truth is, I'm still not sure if I loved or hated it - it was the kind of book I know I'll never be able to read again - and at the same time, I will NEVER FORGET!!! 😱😱😱<br><br>📚 “𝐖𝐞 𝐚𝐫𝐞 𝐚𝐥𝐥 𝐠𝐨𝐢𝐧𝐠 𝐭𝐨 𝐝𝐢𝐞, 𝐛𝐮𝐭 𝐠𝐨𝐢𝐧𝐠 𝐭𝐨 𝐝𝐢𝐞 𝐟𝐢𝐫𝐬𝐭. 𝐈𝐧 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐯𝐞𝐫𝐲 𝐥𝐚𝐬𝐭 𝐬𝐞𝐜𝐨𝐧𝐝 𝐨𝐟 𝐦𝐲 𝐥𝐢𝐟𝐞, 𝐈 𝐰𝐢𝐥𝐥 𝐭𝐡𝐢𝐧𝐤 𝐨𝐟 𝐲𝐨𝐮." 📚<br><br>Tarryn doesn't stop to surprise me with her amazing writing and geniuses mind... I loved the insanity, the mystery, that the puzzle pieces slowly revealed a super surprising picture... I loved that the book displayed a different kind of love - but equally powerful... ❤🎠<br><br>The ending was bitter sweet - but it was quite typical "Tarryny ending" - and I wouldn't expect anything else from her!!! 😂<br><br>In summary - I'm having a reading block! (and thanks for that Tarryn, you bitch!) 😭😂<br><br>• I listened to the AUDIO version. 🎧<br><br>▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️▪️▫️<br><br>📖 ᖴOᒪᒪOᗯ ᗰE Oᑎ IᑎᔕTᗩGᖇᗩᗰ: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/the_romantic_blogger/">https://www.instagram.com/the_romanti...</a><br><br>📖 ᐯIᔕIT ᗰY ᗷᒪOG ᖴOᖇ ᗰOᖇE ᖇEᐯIEᗯᔕ: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://books-romance.com/">https://books-romance.com/</a><br><br>📖 GOOᗪᖇEᗩᗪᔕ: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bit.ly/3acMRMP">https://bit.ly/3acMRMP</a><br><br>💕 לקריאת הסקירה בעברית, כנסו לבלוג: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://books-romance.com/">https://books-romance.com/</a> 💕</span>

<div id="review_679145904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679145904" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2127955-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520179670p2/2127955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679145904?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/2127955-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=disappointing-reads">disappointing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=not-what-i-expected">not-what-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2127955-holly?shelf=dark-and-twisted">dark-and-twisted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679145904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10550630621575641403"><b>2 stars</b><br/><br/>God, this is a hard one for me.<br/><br/>I absolutely LOVE Fisher's writing style. It's beautiful and unique and always conjures up various emotions for me. And while the writing in <i>Mud Vein</i> was as gorgeous as ever....the actual story left me feeling cold and detached.<br/><br/>I don't really want to sit here and list all of the problems I had with this book. I actually hate writing negative reviews over all. But, i feel like i need to at least partially explain why it was a struggle for me to even give this</span>
  <span id="freeText10550630621575641403" style="display:none"><b>2 stars</b><br /><br />God, this is a hard one for me.<br /><br />I absolutely LOVE Fisher's writing style. It's beautiful and unique and always conjures up various emotions for me. And while the writing in <i>Mud Vein</i> was as gorgeous as ever....the actual story left me feeling cold and detached.<br /><br />I don't really want to sit here and list all of the problems I had with this book. I actually hate writing negative reviews over all. But, i feel like i need to at least partially explain why it was a struggle for me to even give this book 2 stars.<br /><br />First of all, the premise was very intriguing to me. And even though for the first 30% of the book I was beyond confused as to WTF was going on, I was still willing to go with it...hoping that everything would make sense in the end, and when Fisher gave us the <b>Big Reveal</b> it would wash away all of the frustration I had with the plot.<br /><br />No such luck.<br /><br />The twist...was a <b>HUGE</b> disappointment. It made very little sense, and was just too far fetched for me. And while I never found myself really rooting for the main characters, I still found the actual ending to be quite depressing.<br /><br /><i>Mud Vein</i> was one of my top 3 most anticipated books of 2014, and perhaps some could say that my expectations were too high. Judging by all the glowing reviews I have seen for this book, once again i seem to be in the minority when it comes to my opinion.<br /><br />I am still an enormous fan of Fisher's writing, and even though this book left me disappointed, I will still gladly read anything else she decides to publish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10550630621575641403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_679130857" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679130857" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679130857?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=emotional-angsty-books">emotional-angsty-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679130857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2788208765362012261">So, I'm starting off my review with the letter that TF left her readers and I'm highlighting some very crucial parts. Parts you need to pay careful attention to if you're serious about reading this book.<br/><br/><i>"Dear Reader,<br/>I am a writer and words are my weapon. <b>I want to hurt you</b>. I want my words to be salt, and I want to pour them into your open wound. I want my words to be jagged pieces of mirror that you can see yourself reflected in. I am a sadist otherwise known as an artist. <b>My books are a call t</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText2788208765362012261" style="display:none">So, I'm starting off my review with the letter that TF left her readers and I'm highlighting some very crucial parts. Parts you need to pay careful attention to if you're serious about reading this book.<br><br><i>"Dear Reader,<br>I am a writer and words are my weapon. <b>I want to hurt you</b>. I want my words to be salt, and I want to pour them into your open wound. I want my words to be jagged pieces of mirror that you can see yourself reflected in. I am a sadist otherwise known as an artist. <b>My books are a call to women who have been doubled over by heartache, bound by boredom, captives of a past that will not let them go, victors of a past that tried to kill them</b>. I have a disease you see, it’s called human nature, and I am fascinated by it. So, if you choose to read Mud Vein remember that about me. I’m not writing to entertain you, or to make money, or to have my book propped neatly on a shelf in Target. I write to explore the dark corners of myself, and I want you to come with me. I’m a little bit like you. I think you’ll see yourself in the pages of Mud Vein. I haven’t told you very much about it on purpose. I want you to go in blind. I want you to stumble across a thought, a sound, a hurt-which you had thought special to you. And realize I have felt them too, someone you have never met. If you choose to read Mud Vein, please don’t ask yourself what it says, <b>ask yourself what it means</b>. And once you read my black words, on a white page, e-mail me and tell me your interpretation. I can’t wait for your thoughts.<br><br>Tarryn Fisher"</i><br><br> <br>First off, I liked this book, as in, the writing and at this point, I'm not really sure what else I "liked". My mind is a bit scrambled. But...I LOVE the way TF writes. It's really about <i>all the little things</i> and the way she makes things seem so real. <br><br>Secondly, this book is <i>depressing</i>!! My heart goes out to Senna. I just cannot fathom everything she went through. I would not wish that on my worst enemy. <br><br>Lastly, I couldn't stop reading it! I know not everyone feels the same way but let me explain. I like books I can't figure out and I especially like books that don't always have a happy ending. I knew going in that this would be a given. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397173043i/9242297._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Back to the story... If you've read the blurb, you know that Senna gets kidnapped and kept in a house. What you don't know is that there's someone else with her and it's a person who has helped her in the past, Isaac. <br><br>Isaac is pretty amazing and when he first meets Senna she has already been through some horrible things and then has some horrific things happen to her. He tries to be what she needs but she's a tough cookie to crack. <br><br>The book is broken up into three parts: the part where they are first kidnapped, the part where they meet, and the part after. So obviously, it takes a while to get some answers. You mind will try to figure things out but I will be shocked if you're able. I didn't even come close. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397174131i/9242535.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's where we come to the things I didn't like. I was shocked at who the zookeeper(aka kidnapper) was because it's not anyone you would guess and the reasoning's are pretty flimsy IMO. The only good thing I can say about it is that the person was probably one of the people who could be the least hurtful. (if that makes sense)<br><br>I loved the Love me with Lies series especially <i>The Opportunist</i>. I love how TF takes little ordinary things and make them so <i>un</i>ordinary. The music without words, the white, and knowing people by their sense...I just loved all that. <br><br>As you've guessed, this isn't a book for everybody, most of my friends either loved it or didn't like it/DNF'd it. It's really important for you to have a good idea what you're getting yourself into because it is one crazy trip! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397323494i/9263085.jpg" width="400" height="070" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Favorite quotes:</u>
</b><br><br>♥ "Acceptance. Embrace the suck." <br><br>♥ "No one wants to carry someone when they're heavy from life."<br><br>♥ "Why are you here?" <br><br>"Because you are."<br><br>♥ " He kissed me with color, with drumbeat, and a surgeon’s precision. He kissed me with who he was, the sum of his life—and it was all encompassing. I wondered what I kissed him with since I was only broken parts."<br><br>♥ “The truth is for the mind,” he says. “Lies are for the heart. So let’s just keep lying.”<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2788208765362012261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679062611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14712215406266440218"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396537867i/9148827._SX540_.jpg' width='475.06' height='191.29' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>One of the best books I’ve ever read. Powerful. Introspective. Suspenseful. Gripping. Heartbreaking. An emotional powerhouse perfectly crafted and brilliantly written.<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“It’s your darkness that pulls me in. Your mud vein. But sometimes having a mud vein will kill you.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>I experienced this book, alone, in a quiet house on a rainy day, which I felt was ominously appropriate. A dark, cold day listening to the melodic spattering of rain as the words from this story battered my thoughts more forceful</span>
  <span id="freeText14712215406266440218" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396537867i/9148827._SX540_.jpg" width="475.06" height="191.29" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of the best books I’ve ever read. Powerful. Introspective. Suspenseful. Gripping. Heartbreaking. An emotional powerhouse perfectly crafted and brilliantly written.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“It’s your darkness that pulls me in. Your mud vein. But sometimes having a mud vein will kill you.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I experienced this book, alone, in a quiet house on a rainy day, which I felt was ominously appropriate. A dark, cold day listening to the melodic spattering of rain as the words from this story battered my thoughts more forcefully. Gripped me. I was immediately taken. Held captive myself, by the raw power of this book. The trickling of information, clues, truths, secrets, all half-exposed, half-shrouded as the story unfurled. It’s difficult to convey what this story is about, but I think the best, most succinct word I can use is truth.<br><br>This is a story about truth.<br><br>The truth we seek to uncover. The truth beneath the pain. The truth we bury deep inside and are too blind to see. And finally, the truth we find … often times, too late.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“This is a game, and if I want to get out, I have to find the truth.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Senna awakes to a real-life nightmare. She finds herself imprisoned without chains, but locked up in a cabin encased by snow, trapped with a person from her past who ignites old feelings she meant to keep dormant. Unclear clues taunt all around them. The game is ingeniously staged for them to figure out. There are many facets to this story, ribbons of the plot untwining gradually, and during this part of the book, I found myself caught up in the suspense of their situation. I found myself observing and deliberating, elements twisting and clicking into place. Waiting. Watching for the nuances of their environment, clues hidden in the subtext of words and hiding in plain sight.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Who will live and who will die? It’s the worst form of torture a person can imagine — the wait to die.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>But the more I worked to decipher the mystery, the more I found myself intrigued by the enigma that is Senna. I was lost in her, unraveling her complexities to better understand her essence. She defies normal, reveling in the anti-current of society. She’s a writer. An artist. She takes in the world through a different lens. She’s also one of the most tragic characters of which I’ve read. Pain has defined her. Abandonment has shaped her. She destroys before she can be destroyed. But the more I tried to untangle, the more I wondered whether perhaps I was trying to uncover something that already laid bare. To me, she was both exceedingly vulnerable and entirely shielded. She’s worked so hard to smother the sum of her painful experiences that she lives behind the haze of a thin veil, obscuring her emotions. There’s only been one person who’s been able to lift the fog and see right through her.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“She can’t see the landscape anymore. It’s all painted in her grief.”</blockquote>
</b><br> ---(Florence and The Machine, Landscape)<br><br>Dr. Isaac Asterholder. This is the man she finds in the cabin … the man from her past … the man she pushed away. He met Senna in a moment of chaos and vulnerability, in the raging aftermath of pain. He forced his way into her life, helping her in a way no one had before.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Isaac was a stranger and he had seen more of my wounds than anyone else. Not because I chose him… He was just always there. That’s what scared me.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>We are transported back to a time where we can better understand Senna and Isaac and the charged dynamic between them. Isaac pushed through all the walls that Senna erected, but he never pushed too far, just far enough to make progress. He was her lifeline at a time her life seemed to permanently dim. Senna’s way of dealing with life was seeing what happened as an indisputable fact. Something she just had to deal with. She was broken. Disfigured by fate and circumstance. She didn’t relent to the pain, but she saw herself as permanently scarred. Isaac was selfless, fixated on healing those broken parts of her he could, bringing color, feeling and intensity to a life painted white, stark and cold. A person from Senna’s past said that she was a “daughter of winter” and I think if she personified winter, then Isaac was someone who thrived in the cold uncertainty of the season. He was a fixer who understood more about her wounds and her silence than anyone else. He carried her pain as his own.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“He kissed me with color, with drumbeat, and a surgeon’s precision. He kissed me with who he was, the sum of his life — and it was all encompassing. I wondered what I kissed him with since I was only broken parts.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Nevertheless, peering into their past didn’t change reality. They were now two people with lives that had long diverged, suddenly so tangled again by a situation they never expected. Trying to survive a looming danger, an anonymous culprit, the pangs of hunger and the insanity of time, was enough to break open the floodgates, bringing a deluge of emotions that Senna had worked so hard to suppress.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Being stuck on love was a real bitch to cure. Like cancer, I think. Just when you think you’re over it, it comes back.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>What happens in the cabin and the events that lead up to it are for you to experience. These characters are just brilliantly written, each on their own journey to find their truth. As a writer, Senna needed “simplicity to create complexity,” but I think that she was so lost in her own complexity that she couldn’t see the simple truth in front of her. She was paralyzed by fear – of so many things – but also to feel so much and have it all be brutally taken away. Because Isaac was all feeling. He flooded her senses. And Senna was afraid to feel. Feeling meant being tethered to someone, beholden to something she couldn’t control.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“There is a string that connects us that is not visible to the eye… Maybe every person has more than one soul they are connected to, and all over the world there are these invisible strings…. Maybe the chances that you’ll find each and every one of your soulmates is slim. But sometimes you’re lucky enough to stumble across one. And you feel a tug. And it’s not so much a choice to love them through their flaws and through your differences, but rather you love them without even trying. You love their flaws.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>This is one of the best books I’ve ever read. Absolutely and undeniably brilliantly written. The syntax. The word choices. The layers and sub-layers of meaning make it impossible to not get mesmerized by the story. To me, it felt like a multisensory experience. As if I were walking into a literary butterfly den, not knowing whether to get lost in the beauty of the colorful patterns, or entranced by the soft sounds fluttering in the distance, or be flooded by the smell of the environment around you. I felt my way through this book. I was captivated by all the elements coming together so perfectly. Powerfully. It honestly just blew me away. Is this a romance? No. It’s a novel that defies genre. It’s fiction, suspense, romance, mystery all woven together to create an unforgettable story about discovering the darkest, muddiest, well-buried truths within ourselves… the kind of truth that fills a life with meaning and ultimately sets you free.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You’ve been silent your whole life. You were silent when we met, silent when you suffered. Silent when life kept hitting you… I tried to move you. It didn’t work. But that doesn’t mean you didn’t move me. I heard everything you didn’t say. I heard it so loudly that I couldn’t shut if off. Your silence, Senna, I hear it so loudly.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381417425i/4836951._SX540_.png" width="361.33" height="228.67" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>For more reviews, connect with me: <br><a href="www.vilmasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Vilma's Book Blog</a> | <a href="www.facebook.com/chitchatbookblog" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="www.twitter.com/vilmairis" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14712215406266440218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_899734924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer899734924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17835319636877409269">This book was beautifully written and I would definitely read more books by this author. Unfortunately, I didn't love this book like I was expecting to. I never really felt like I connected with Senna at all, maybe as a result of her being so emotionally detached for most of the book. Not having that attachment, I never did fall in love with the story. It was "ok" overall, even though the writing and complex plot twists were absolutely superb. I really think the only thing stopping me from lovin</span>
  <span id="freeText17835319636877409269" style="display:none">This book was beautifully written and I would definitely read more books by this author. Unfortunately, I didn't love this book like I was expecting to. I never really felt like I connected with Senna at all, maybe as a result of her being so emotionally detached for most of the book. Not having that attachment, I never did fall in love with the story. It was "ok" overall, even though the writing and complex plot twists were absolutely superb. I really think the only thing stopping me from loving this book was the fact that I didn't really like, or relate to Senna at all.<br /><br />Aside from Senna, this book had everything that I love in a book. It was very well-written, with a lot of mystery and suspense. Isaac was a great character and I felt much more connected to him throughout the book. The ending and the revelation of the zookeeper's identity was totally unpredictable, which doesn't happen very often. I felt that the ending was fitting and seemed consistent with the glum mood of the book. <br /><br />This is not your standard romance. If you are looking for a hot, passionate tale, this isn't it. It is emotionally and psychologically deep mystery/suspense with a background love story. <br /><br />I would recommend giving this book a try, even though it wasn't one that I loved. <br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_679069402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679069402" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679069402?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Varian Krylov</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ash Wednesday by: </span>
      Buddy Read with Ana Rita
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=head-trip">head-trip</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679069402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16079391660919261073"><i>
  <b>3 STARS<br/><blockquote>”You are at once both the quiet and the confusion of my heart.”<br/>-Franz Kafka</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>I couldn’t choose a quote from this book, so we’ll go with that one.<br/><br/>Well this certainly wouldn’t be a crowd pleaser. But something about an author as established as Tarryn Fisher refusing to pander to certain limits and expectations makes me want to outright slap a 5 star rating on <i>Mud Vein</i>. Something about seeing her unmistakable fingerprints all over a book that is such a departure from the comforts set by a </span>
  <span id="freeText16079391660919261073" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>3 STARS<br><blockquote>”You are at once both the quiet and the confusion of my heart.”<br>-Franz Kafka</blockquote></b>
</i><br>I couldn’t choose a quote from this book, so we’ll go with that one.<br><br>Well this certainly wouldn’t be a crowd pleaser. But something about an author as established as Tarryn Fisher refusing to pander to certain limits and expectations makes me want to outright slap a 5 star rating on <i>Mud Vein</i>. Something about seeing her unmistakable fingerprints all over a book that is such a departure from the comforts set by a series as successful as <i>Love Me With Lies</i> just clenches at my heart. <br><br>Because seriously, I know its a personal question and all but what’s the level of meta in this book? On a scale of <i>Wheel of Fortune</i> to <i>Community</i>?<br><br>It was far from perfect, but in more ways than one, this was a more believable progression from <i>The Opportunist</i> and <i>Dirty Red</i> than <i>Thief</i> for me. Sometimes I even felt the ghosts of Caleb and Olivia in Isaac and Senna. Their dynamic eerily reminiscent but also distinct: a woman broken by the world and the man who loves her ugly, jagged pieces, this time within a psychological thriller milieu. I really wasn’t invested in the whole mystery early on, despite it being this book’s take-off point. I was more interested in the complexity of both characters who were both strangers and non-strangers at the beginning of the story. My curiosity on who did it did eventually kick in once their backstory was satisfied and while I never really considered it as the driving force behind the plot, I found myself happy with how this was resolved. What others may read as anticlimactic, I’m inclined to interpret as not being the climax at all.<br><br>Because this wasn’t a book about a woman and a man who got abducted in the middle of nowhere after all.<br><br>Senna was a bit of a painful character to experience. She has a lot of brambles entwined in the complex mess of her twigs and branches while her roots extend to depths of fathomless, unanswered whys. She’s an Emilie Autumn quote: “a terribly real thing in a terribly false world causing her so much pain.” She is all of us and none of us. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>She was a house with no windows.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>There’s even an almost fantastical quality to her relationship with Isaac and her path to her truth with enough emotional textures worthy of Wong Kar-Wai and Lars von Trier's wistful pain. It was all very cinematic, the circumstances too unnatural and out there that didn’t quite fit with the truthiness it was trying to convey.<br><br>This has been a particular trademark of this author, of course, one that endeared me to the stories she weaved before. Ultimately, the themes of conditional and unconditional love were explored with exhaustive depth and complexity, but the twinge of disappointment over insta-love as the bottomline was undeniable from where I stand. <br><br>I also can’t help but notice some heavy handedness everywhere including the prose and dialogue. I’m hard-pressed to quote this book. There are just too many. It read like one sound bite after another, the subtext in the dialogue alone was relentlessly cryptic. And placed within a psychological thriller-slash-mystery, it just got too exhausting and monotonously depressing. A problem I’ve had before with Varian Krylov: there’s not enough room to let the story exhale for a moment, to contrast or to create space to fill up again with emotions. Melancholia bleeding into melancholia equals emotional fatigue. <br><br>It was in that monotony that I felt this book ultimately lost its grasp on me. Such that somewhere past the middle, the pieces only made sense within the context of that moment. But gaining some distance and perspective you lose sight of things, miss out certain details in the murky depths of depression, metaphors and subtext, and before you know it you're thinking of the the Chrysler Building fighting against a radically religious shrimp while a confused crystal bird looks on.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396879412i/9197747._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Yes that was a gratuitously placed image, I just wanted to put that somewhere because revisiting my thoughts on this book was depressing enough.)<br><br>I really really wanted to fall in love with this because the sentiment was heartfelt and I liked the feeling of reading something that felt written with bone-rattling, visceral honesty and balls-to-the-wall passion without catering to anyone’s comfort zones. It's just that the heaviness just fuzzed out some of its edge, robbing <i>Mud Vein</i> a bit of its brilliance. But in terms of direction and evolution from this author, this was a welcome comfort.<br><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/845148/monotony-in-melancholia" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on Booklikes.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16079391660919261073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_679071350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679071350" />
    <a title=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog"><img alt=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486609762p2/2607684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679071350?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" href="/user/show/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog"> Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679071350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4211863344959553216"><a href='http://bit.ly/1i7wY6L' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398091156i/9366411._SX540_.jpg' alt='Review — Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>5 stars</b><br/><br/><em>Mud Vein</em> is a life changing book. It is a book that you don't read, you absorb it. You savor it. Tarryn Fisher's words spoke to me, the deepest part of me. After I finished this book, I couldn't even move on to something else. Instead, I immediately reread it. <em>Mud Vein</em> left me with this indescribable feeling that I don't want to wash off with other words. Instead, I want to keep swimming in the sea of Senna Richards and her darkness. <em>Mud Vein</em> is one of my <strong>all-time favorite books</strong>.<br/><br/>Tarry</span>
  <span id="freeText4211863344959553216" style="display:none"><a href="http://bit.ly/1i7wY6L" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398091156i/9366411._SX540_.jpg" alt="Review — Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>5 stars</b><br><br><em>Mud Vein</em> is a life changing book. It is a book that you don't read, you absorb it. You savor it. Tarryn Fisher's words spoke to me, the deepest part of me. After I finished this book, I couldn't even move on to something else. Instead, I immediately reread it. <em>Mud Vein</em> left me with this indescribable feeling that I don't want to wash off with other words. Instead, I want to keep swimming in the sea of Senna Richards and her darkness. <em>Mud Vein</em> is one of my <strong>all-time favorite books</strong>.<br><br>Tarryn Fisher's intention is for the reader to go into this book completely blind, which is why the synopsis is somewhat vague. I will keep my review spoiler-free so that you have the best reading experience.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"Maybe the chances that you'll find each and every one of your soulmates is slim. But sometimes you're lucky enough to stumble across one. And you feel a tug. And it's not so much a choice to love them through their flaws and through your difference but rather you love them without even trying. You love their flaws."</em>
</blockquote><br><em>Mud Vein </em>is a story about a woman's journey to find the truth, her truth. On her thirty-third birthday, Senna Richards awakens in a mysterious room. It doesn't take long for her to realize that she's been drugged and kidnapped. Peering out the window, she sees "all the snow in the world," tipping her off that she's far, far away from her Seattle home. <em>
  <strong>And she is not</strong>
</em><strong><em> alone</em>.</strong> She's trapped in the cabin with the one person from her past that painted her black and white world with color, the one person she fought so hard to push away.<br><br>Senna Richards is one of the most heartbreaking yet captivating characters I have ever read. Her past holds her prisoner. Bound by hurt, abandonment and self-destruction, she holds the reins to her emotions, to her surroundings, and to all people she chooses to let in and out of her life. She writes to the tune of white and black walls, to music with no words, and boxes away any feeling at all so that she doesn't have to feel pain.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"Things distracted me. Or maybe they complicated me. I didn't like to live with color. I wasn't always like that. I learned to survive better."</em>
</blockquote><br>I fell for Senna Richards. I fell for her darkness and the shards of light that peeked through her cracks. I fell for her vulnerability and her strength. Perhaps most the most tragic thing about her is that she was blind to the truth that was right in front her. Fisher takes you on an emotional journey through Senna's past, through the pain and through her hurt.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"You've been silent your whole life. You were silent when we met, silent when you sufferent. Silent when life kept hitting you. I was like that too, a little. But not like you. You are a stillness. And I tried to move you. It didn't work. But that doesn't mean you didn't move me. I heard everything you didn't say. I heard it so loudly that I couldn't shut it off. Your silence, Senna. I hear it so loudly."</em>
</blockquote><br>Her life of isolation is put to the test when she is reacquainted with the one person from her past that fills her with color, sound and feeling. Isaac Asterholder holds onto a piece of Senna's past that she tried so desperately to bury deep, lock away, and forget about. Isaac is Senna's fellow captor in the cabin in the middle of nowhere. Senna met Isaac at moment of time in her life when she was falling in every sense of the word. He carried her burdens for her.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"Birds are the only things that grow wings. We're just left to muck through the mire like a bunch of emotional cave men."<br>"Now if you have someone to carry you."</em>
</blockquote><br>Fisher's intentional style of storytelling gripped me from the very beginning. The way in which she reveals Senna's story was perfectly executed and exquisitely timed. The most incredible thing about this book is what it does to your heart. I could feel every fear, moment of anger, intense feelings of love, painful hunger and sadness that Senna felt. This book made me feel not only for the characters but for myself. <i>Mud Vein </i>made me look at myself and my life. This book has words on the surface but it has a pulse and it has a heartbeat. It is living and breathing and its veins hook straight into your heart.<br><br>If I had to recommend one book to you this year, it would be this one. This book is an experience you need to have.<br><br><em>
  <strong>* I received a copy from the author in exchange for an honest review</strong>
</em><br><br> <br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/1i7wY6L" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398091156i/9366412._SY540_.jpg" alt="Review — Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><strong>Find more of my reviews &amp; other bookish things here:<br><br>✥ <a href="http://bit.ly/1i7wY6L" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read the Review on the Blog</a><br>✥ My blog <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Reading Books Like a Boss</a><br>✥ Like on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/ReadingBooksLikeABoss" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a><br>✥ Follow on <a href="http://twitter.com/ireadlikeaboss" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br>✥ Subscribe by <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.us10.list-manage.com/subscribe/post?u=e1db0261647306d53aef66844&amp;id=e10ebb3cc7" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Email</a><br></strong><br>✥ MUD VEIN was one of my <a href="http://bit.ly/1cbHHu2" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>most anticipated books of 2014!!</b>
</a><br><a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419361462i/13045882.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>4/6/2014 - Mud Vein is not only a top favorite of 2014 but an ALL-TIME favorite read. Everyone needs to experience this book!!! Review to come!!</b><br><br>SYNOPSIS:<br><b>When reclusive novelist Senna Richards wakes up on her thirty-third birthday, everything has changed. Caged behind an electrical fence, locked in a house in the middle of the snow, Senna is left to decode the clues to find out why she was taken. If she wants her freedom, she has to take a close look at her past. But, her past has a heartbeat…and her kidnapper is nowhere to be found. With her survival hanging by a thread, Senna soon realizes this is a game. A dangerous one. Only the truth can set her free.</b><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380430762i/863815._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't wait! I can't wait! I will read anything Tarryn Fisher writes because she is a word magician!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4211863344959553216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194522493" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194522493?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=own-it-spent-my-food-money-on-it">own-it-spent-my-food-money-on-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194522493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12068638938704664907">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423496584ra/13633768.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Ha! Just kidding. Calm down, fangirls. I really had you going there for a minute though, didn’t I? <i>Mud Vein</i> definitely isn’t the worst thing I’ve ever read. Heck, it isn’t even the worst thing I’ve read this week (still looking at you for that one, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190900542?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ted Callahan</a>). I added this book to my TBR because . . . well, mainly because it was only a buck, but also because Tarryn Fisher and Colleen Hoover’s new co-written book was getting lots</span>
  <span id="freeText12068638938704664907" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423496584ra/13633768.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ha! Just kidding. Calm down, fangirls. I really had you going there for a minute though, didn’t I? <i>Mud Vein</i> definitely isn’t the worst thing I’ve ever read. Heck, it isn’t even the worst thing I’ve read this week (still looking at you for that one, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1190900542?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Ted Callahan</a>). I added this book to my TBR because . . . well, mainly because it was only a buck, but also because Tarryn Fisher and Colleen Hoover’s new co-written book was getting lots of hype (both positive and negative) and I wanted to give one of Ms. Fisher’s solo works a chance before I committed to either read or never read <i>Never Never</i>.<br><br>If you follow my reviews you know that I read a little bit of everything, but I will say that NA or whatever the f they are calling it today isn’t generally my genre of choice. When I saw <i>Mud Vein</i> shelved as “dark” and “suspense” and “thriller” and those shelves were accompanied by ranting and raving by fans, non-fans, <i>and</i> the author all talking about how this story was apparently super disturbing to some, I figured it could be a winner for me. <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423496584ra/13633769.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yeah. I guess I like my “dark” like fucking pitch black without even a sliver of light showing through. Although <i>Mud Vein</i> is the story of a reclusive author and her former <s>stalker</s> doctor discovering they have been kidnapped and apparently left for dead in a cabin in the Alaskan wilderness, it didn’t really get psychologically thriller-y enough for me.<br><br><b>KIND OF A SPOILER AHEAD, SO TURN BACK NOW IF YOU DON’T WANT ME TELLING YOU WHO <i>WASN’T</i> THE BAD GUY.</b><br><br>Still Here? Okay, I know this wasn’t <b>my</b> book and it’s not my call who the bad guy is, but with all the hype I <i>really</i> wanted it to be Isaac. If he was a big enough nutbag to basically move himself in to Senna’s house when the “superbadawful” happened, why wouldn’t he be the one who locked her up with him in isolation until she admitted the “truth”????? But maybe that’s just me . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423496584ra/13633770.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’m giving this one 2.5 Stars because it was a perfectly average read for me. I thought Tarryn Fisher did a quality job of keeping the momentum of the story going, especially when it was very much driven by the inner workings of Senna’s head rather than via conversation. I will warn you, though, Ms. Fisher is a lover of language. If you are a reader who gets annoyed by 50 words being used where 5 would suffice (*cough* like in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/712254473?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Tahereh Mafi </a> books *cough*), there’s a good chance this one won’t work for you. But when the words are written well . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“He was right there, making me look at him. His gaze was slicing. Sluicing. There was too much emotion. He kissed me with color, with drumbeat, and a surgeon’s precision. He kissed me with who he was, the sum of his life – and it was all encompassing.”</i>
</b><br><br>Sometimes it’s okay for there to be lots of them.<br><br>Oh, and dare I forget to mention the soundtrack chosen for this one. References to Awolnation and my most beloved Florence (as well as her Machine) really helped suck me in to the story.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Your song reminds me of swimming, which somehow I’d forgot.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423496584ra/13633771.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I want to be Florence Welch when I grow up.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12068638938704664907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_679110959" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679110959" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679110959?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renee" href="/user/show/12732363-renee">Renee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12732363-renee?shelf=6-star-rating-loved-it-rare-epic">6-star-rating-loved-it-rare-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12732363-renee?shelf=favorite-author">favorite-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679110959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11151101038849145368"><b>**** 6 STARS ****</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b> “What’s the difference?” I asked him. “Between the love of your life, and your soul mate?”<br/><br/>“One is a choice, and one is not.” </b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301175.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> <i>
  <b>“You are my truth”. </b>
</i><br/><br/><br/><i>
  <b>This book....</b>
</i> *swallows hard* <i>this book</i> cut deep and left a scar in its wake.<br/><br/>I said it in my <b>Love Me With Lies series</b> review and I’m going to say it again....<b>Tarryn Fisher's</b> writing is so raw, rare, elegant and rhythmical -it penetrates through to your skin, runs through your veins and pierces your heart. It flows so natur</span>
  <span id="freeText11151101038849145368" style="display:none"><b>**** 6 STARS ****</b><br><br><i>
  <b> “What’s the difference?” I asked him. “Between the love of your life, and your soul mate?”<br><br>“One is a choice, and one is not.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301175.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <i>
  <b>“You are my truth”. </b>
</i><br><br><br><i>
  <b>This book....</b>
</i> *swallows hard* <i>this book</i> cut deep and left a scar in its wake.<br><br>I said it in my <b>Love Me With Lies series</b> review and I’m going to say it again....<b>Tarryn Fisher's</b> writing is so raw, rare, elegant and rhythmical -it penetrates through to your skin, runs through your veins and pierces your heart. It flows so naturally and it’s so addictive that it will leave you desperately hungry for more. You will find yourself rereading each sentence over and over and over again. I wanted absorb it all in, in hope of storing those words for keepsake in my memory bank. I had to restrain myself from highlighting the entire book and quoting it in my status updates. Her words demand you to feel, live and breath her story. Her effortless writing is infused with class, smoothness, sexiness and a whole lot of wicked.. I just *love* her work.<br><br><i>
  <b> “There is a string that connects us that is not visible to the eye. Maybe every person has more than one soul they are connected to, and all over the world there are those invisible strings… Maybe the chances that you’ll find each and every one of your soul mates is slim. But sometimes you’re lucky enough to stumble across one. And you feel a tug. And it’s not so much a choice to love them though their flaws and through your differences, but rather you love them without even trying. You love their flaws.” </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301174.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There is love in this story but there is no romance. It is so much deeper than that. If you are going into this expecting a fluffy hearts and flowers type of read, where boy meets girl, they fall in love and live happily ever after then think again. If that’s what you want then don’t read it - it not for you, but I must say you will be missing out on a brilliant book and <i> Oh what a shame that would be!</i>. This book is raw, its real and it speaks the truth. Not everything in life is rainbows, ponies and sunshine. For many, it is darkness and cold. This book gives us the rare opportunity as avid readers to explore and ‘feel’ that dark side to a characters life. It’s not exaggerated or unrealistic, it just.... is. It’s perfect within its imperfections and it is a story that left me with more than a few new grey hairs.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612527i/9301250.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>My advice to you is to pay very close attention to detail when reading this– take notes if you must. Tarryn sets up the puzzle but it is our job to put the pieces together. That’s what I love most about her work; it’s that you need to actual think. It’s not just about sitting back and enjoying the ride. She actually forces you not get involved in the story and discovery process.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612406i/9301228.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is about the suffering, loss, fear of love/life and the consequences of enduring all those things. I don’t want to give away too much of the story, to really appreciate and feel the story it’s best to go in completely blind and allow it to overtake you completely.<br><br>I felt as though <b>Tarryn</b> was holding my heart in the palm of her hand the entire time and just kept squeezing and squeezing- she had no mercy. With every turn of the page she would add just a little more pressure until the very end when she completely disintegrated my heart.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301176._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Tarryn fisher</i> has a distinct way of cracking your chest open, baring your soul, ripping your heart out, stomping on it and in that single second before you feel like you’re about to take your last breath she shoves it back in your chest. You survive, but your heart will never be the same again. She is an extraordinarily gifted author, who not only thinks outside the box but also challenges the reader to do the same. The originality and uniqueness of her work will leave you speechless and awe struck. The effort that she has put into her work is evident through the flawless details and the well thought out puzzles. <br><br><i>
  <b>"If you formed a woman's soul out of black graphite, bathed it in blood, and then rolled it around in the softest rose petals, you still wouldn't have touched on the complication that was my match".</b>
</i><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301177.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Note to Author....</b><br><br><i>Tarryn Fisher</i>... In one of your blogs you said something about <i>
  <b>“Wanting to hurt us with your words”. </b>
</i>Mission accomplished. What happens when you pour salt water on a wound? It <i>burns, stings and hurts like hell</i> and sometimes it even leaves a scar. Yes, your words hurt, but there is also a power in them that heals.<br><br><i>
  <b>"You are stillness. And I tried to move you. It didn't work. But that doesn't mean you didn't move me. I heard everything you didn't say. I heard it so loudly that I couldn't shut it off. Your silence, Senna, I hear it so loudly".</b>
</i><br><br><br><b>
  <i>"Landscape" and “Cosmic Love” By Florence and the Machine </i>
</b> are the songs to listen to while reading Mud Vein. <i>Tarryn Fisher</i> mentions them throughout the book often.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301179._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301180._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Three things cannot be long hidden: the sun, the moon, and the truth.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397612124i/9301173._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>“Why are you here?”......<br><br><br><i>“Because you are”.</i></b><br><br><br><br><br>03.14<br><b>Confession</b>... <i>I totally have a girl crush on Tarryn Fisher!!!! Seriously is it the 18th of April yet?????? I <b>WANT. NEED. MUST HAVE. WOULD HURT PEOPLE</b> TO HAVE THIS <u>BOOK</u> RIGHT NOW!!!!!! </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396585373ra/9156570.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>07.13 - I would read A.N.Y.T.H.I.N.G Tarryn Fisher writes - Pure Perfection! She's in a league of her own! Bring it on!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11151101038849145368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Angela Richardson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14805495-angela-richardson"><img alt="Angela Richardson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459652982p2/14805495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679144978?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela Richardson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela Richardson" href="/user/show/14805495-angela-richardson">Angela Richardson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679144978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11054312169801512352">Superbly written. I was dying to know how who/why/how from the very beginning and it kept me guessing the entire time. Did I like the ending...no. But I understand why it ended that way. The message is beautiful, dark and thought provoking. There is so much you can take away from this book on a very positive emotional level. But...In saying that, I didn't cry or feel very effected. Perhaps cause when we came to the big reveal, I thought it would have a lot more impact, a different reason or spin</span>
  <span id="freeText11054312169801512352" style="display:none">Superbly written. I was dying to know how who/why/how from the very beginning and it kept me guessing the entire time. Did I like the ending...no. But I understand why it ended that way. The message is beautiful, dark and thought provoking. There is so much you can take away from this book on a very positive emotional level. But...In saying that, I didn't cry or feel very effected. Perhaps cause when we came to the big reveal, I thought it would have a lot more impact, a different reason or spin...or perhaps because I had a darker twist already forming in my head for that moment. So when it was revealed... I was like oh...Okay...Ummmm, right.<br />Still, I can't get past how brilliant the writing is. I couldn't put this story down and was drawn to every sentence and every word.<br />It's five stars from me...although, I'll never be reading it again, even with its very powerful message. Real life is already depressing enough. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681035469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13380560653124776950">I recently read a memoir that climbed its way to the top of my favorites, so of course I wanted to reread my longtime favorite to reevaluate where they both stand. I'm happy to say that this still lives up there. Even the second time around it hit me like a ton of bricks. The insights, the perspectives--this book is special. There are few books that are markers, and what I mean by that is a book that marks a clear before and after in my life because of reading it. I feel different after reading </span>
  <span id="freeText13380560653124776950" style="display:none">I recently read a memoir that climbed its way to the top of my favorites, so of course I wanted to reread my longtime favorite to reevaluate where they both stand. I'm happy to say that this still lives up there. Even the second time around it hit me like a ton of bricks. The insights, the perspectives--this book is special. There are few books that are markers, and what I mean by that is a book that marks a clear before and after in my life because of reading it. I feel different after reading the words. After all, as Janet Fitch once wrote, [words] become the marrow in your bones, making you impervious to the worlds' soft decay.<br /><br /><br />Initial review:<br />Whoa. That book was refreshing in the most contradictory way possible--I loved that it wasn't a romance, but that it was brutally honest about love, and especially the huge psychological game that <i> is </i> Mud Vein.</span>

<div id="review_2151323064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2151323064" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2151323064?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781533093806" href="/book/show/30178115-mud-vein">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151323064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4517455043599875024"><i>Mud Vein</i> is the story of a bestselling author who awakes on her 33rd birthday to find herself having been abducted and trapped in a secluded house, stocked with food, supplies, and the man who saved her years ago... but there's no way out, and no explanation. Just snow, and silence.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>It wasn't like me, but everything had changed. And if he kept showing up for me, I could show up for him. Just this once.</i>
</blockquote><br/>→ <b>
  <i>Senna</i>
</b> ←<br/>Senna is such an incredible and unique narrator. She is cold, stone cold - brut</span>
  <span id="freeText4517455043599875024" style="display:none"><i>Mud Vein</i> is the story of a bestselling author who awakes on her 33rd birthday to find herself having been abducted and trapped in a secluded house, stocked with food, supplies, and the man who saved her years ago... but there's no way out, and no explanation. Just snow, and silence.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>It wasn't like me, but everything had changed. And if he kept showing up for me, I could show up for him. Just this once.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>Senna</i>
</b> ←<br />Senna is such an incredible and unique narrator. She is cold, stone cold - brutally so. She's been hurt, and her defense is to shut people out - and we see that all the time in stories, but I've never seen anyone so committed to the cause as she is. Her choices are downright frustrating at times because they hurt so much to watch unfold, but I related so strongly to something inside of her. I have a horrible habit of disassociating and shutting people out, especially those who love me most, and overcoming that tendency is one of the most difficult challenges I ever have, or ever will, face. It's something I still work on, and seeing it laid out on paper was so eye-opening, because some of the things she said... I felt like I was looking at myself from the outside, and that is such a bizarre place to be, really.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Love sticks, and it stays and it braves the bullshit.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>Isaac</i>
</b> ←<br />What can I even say about Dr. Isaac Asterholder? He is so precious, and kind, and brave, and wonderful. His care is more than Senna thinks she deserves, but he is unwavering, determined to save her one more time. He is the perfect example of a loved one that is trying so desperately to climb the walls that she's put up in defense, no matter how many times the grit peels the skin from his palms.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I should have stayed home. I should have done anything but jog that trail, on that morning, at that time.</i>
</blockquote><br />→ <b>
  <i>trauma</i>
</b> ←<br />Senna undergoes so many brutal moments in her life, and the depiction given of her trauma is literal perfection. Her coping techniques are varied and sometimes unexpected, such as the need for white rooms and music without words, but they never feel as though they're written in to simply serve as plot devices; from cover to cover, Senna feels like a <i>real, authentic</i> human being telling us her story.<br /><br />→ <b>
  <i>final thoughts</i>
</b> ←<br />This book comes with a <i>lot</i> of trigger warnings. It's a tough read, involving rape, cancer, self-harm, and mental health struggles. There is a scene in this book that broke me. I've never known firsthand what it is to watch the person you care most about hurt themselves. Tarryn manages to put that feeling - the agony and helplessness - into words on paper. This scene forced me to evaluate a darkness I try too hard to hide, and I swear, it changed something inside of me. It made me think, for the first time in my life, that maybe I can beat this thing. That it's a thing worth beating.<br /><br />I know this isn't what you came to this review for, and I'm sorry for rambling, but I needed to emphasize how much this story touched me. How much I needed it. I adored this book, and I would recommend it to anyone, so long as you're in the right head-space for how heavy the content is. I know this is a polarizing read, but I can't fathom having not loved it. I know I'll be reading more from Tarryn in the future... once my heart heals from this story, that is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4517455043599875024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9522526349908121392"><b>3 Mind-blowing Stars</b>	<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380421371ra/836928.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I will not tell you the story of this book. Just read the blurb. <br/>This is one of those books that will mess with your emotions in such a big way, that you have to dive in knowing the less possible… believe me, it will enhance your reading experience in a way that will leave you emotionally naked and mind-blown. <br/>Just avoid as much spoilers as you possibly can before read it.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388683472i/7901653.jpg' width='350' height='170' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> <b>Rating: </b> 3 Stars.<br/> <b>Storyline: </b> I’m not the biggest fan of dark stories that mess with a much hidden part</span>
  <span id="freeText9522526349908121392" style="display:none"><b>3 Mind-blowing Stars</b>	<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380421371ra/836928.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I will not tell you the story of this book. Just read the blurb. <br>This is one of those books that will mess with your emotions in such a big way, that you have to dive in knowing the less possible… believe me, it will enhance your reading experience in a way that will leave you emotionally naked and mind-blown. <br>Just avoid as much spoilers as you possibly can before read it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388683472i/7901653.jpg" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Rating: </b> 3 Stars.<br> <b>Storyline: </b> I’m not the biggest fan of dark stories that mess with a much hidden part of the human behavior and messes up with emotions in such a crazy way (Believe me, three or four pages after the beginning and I already had to control the urge to bite my nails!!). There are a lot of books of this type that everyone loved and I was just: “meh”. But somehow Tarry Fisher is always a win for me. I love how can she creates such “out-of-the-box” worlds and I will love them every damn time. If you never read anything from this author, this book would be a great way to start. <br>This wasn't near as good as her previous books, but it was still a nice reading within its genre. <br> <b>Writing Style: </b> First person, female POV. Raw, dark and completely addictive.<br> <b>Character Development: </b> Senna was a little hard for me to like in the beginning, but with time I ended up being somewhat fond of her. I really can’t tell you about the other characters, it would spoil too much, but they add a great depth to the book. <br><b>HEA: </b>	<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Well, not really. But I wasn’t expecting one either. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
